Western Cuisine Industry Union Requests Dissolution 152

Striking Workers Completely Unemployed

Mediation Ineffective, Seeking Other Livelihoods

All workers in the Western cuisine industry in this city have been on strike for several months due to treatment conditions. After repeated mediation by Party and government agencies, the capitalists unreasonably refused, resulting in no solution. All striking workers have therefore lost their jobs and have no means of appeal. The union's entire board of directors and supervisors has tried their best to maintain the situation, but to no avail. They have ordered all workers to seek other livelihoods. The union's entire board of directors and supervisors, Yao Zhongqing, Wu Jingchuan, Wu Shenxiang, Gu Youqing, etc., submitted a document to the Municipal Party Department and the Bureau of Social Affairs, requesting permission to dissolve the union: "We hereby submit the seal, certificate, and expense report, and the membership application to request your review and approval for dissolution. Our members have been oppressed by the capitalists and treated poorly. Therefore, we submitted a request to the capitalists to improve our treatment conditions. Not only did they not sincerely accept and sign the agreement, but they even dared to open and dismiss union members and use various means to destroy the workers' movement, causing all union members to be indignant and go on strike automatically. The capitalists' cunning behaviors and crimes have been exposed in full view. Alas, it is unfortunate for hundreds of union members that the Western Cuisine Industry Union has come to this. Your bureaus have long been aware of the difficult situation and the tricky handling of our union. The directors and supervisors have exhausted their efforts and are unable to sustain the situation. We can only announce to all union members that they should understand and seek other livelihoods. We hereby submit the seal, certificate, and expense report and the membership application for your review and approval to announce the dissolution for public convenience."

The discussions from yesterday are translated and recorded as follows: In addition to the first group which focused on the shipping issue and the second group which focused on the cooperation in international research and discussion, the other groups held discussions about the self criticism of the society itself. Second Level would be the current unofficial discussion but it has to have qualified president. The expert can prepare the committee one week earlier to allow the experts to discuss fully. Choosing the president is very important, due to the benefit and advantage for the president to have expertise on the topic. The conference has improved on the preparation and the collecting of the topics this time. The public meeting and the normal meeting will increase and the party activities should decrease.

County Discovers No Poppy Seedlings Upon Inspection 156

The Shanghai County Government recently received a directive from the Civil Affairs Department, which was forwarded from the Provincial Government, approving the request from the Anti-Opium Committee to strictly enforce the ban on poppy cultivation during this autumn's planting season and to conduct thorough inspections, etc. County Magistrate Yan, upon investigation, found that no poppy seedlings have been planted within the county's borders. Every year, during the spring and autumn seasons, personnel are dispatched to conduct inspections in accordance with the order, and reports are submitted accordingly. This time, Commissioner Fu Dianying was again assigned to conduct inspections in the countryside and to obtain responsible written guarantees from the heads of each district, township, and town for submission and verification. After receiving the order, Commissioner Fu has already visited the six districts under the county's jurisdiction for a week of inspection, and no poppy seedlings were found. Once the written guarantees are collected, a formal report will be submitted.

Central: The Central Bank's 106th Issuance Reserve Inspection Report states: "In accordance with Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations, this association is responsible for inspecting the reserve fund for the issuance of convertible notes of this bank. The announcement is as follows: (A) The total amount of convertible notes issued is 37,841,831 silver dollars, including 34,993,383 silver dollar notes and 2,848,448 subsidiary currency notes. The total amount of the convertible note reserve fund is 37,841,831 silver dollars, including 24,195,990 silver dollars in cash reserve. The cash reserve includes 18,065,905 silver dollars deposited in the bank's issuance vault, 2,548,035 silver dollars deposited in branches in various ports, and 3,582,059 silver dollars deposited in the same industry. The security reserve is equivalent to 13,645,832 silver dollars. (B) The total amount of Chapei convertible notes issued is 1,000,101 yuan. The total amount of the Chapei convertible note reserve fund is 1,000,101 yuan. The reserve fund includes 16,668.35 taels of standard gold, which is converted into Chapei dollars at a fixed price of 60. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank's convertible note regulations, the cash reserve is 60% and the security reserve is 40%. The inspection results show that the cash reserve exceeds 60% and the security reserve is less than 40%, which is consistent with the regulations. This report is hereby made. October 31, 20th year of the Republic of China. Chairman of the Supervisory Board of the Central Bank, Li Fuxun, Supervisors Wang Jingli, Bei Songsun, An Runqing, Yu Zhiqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jiying."

Two Children Run Over by Shanghai-Hangzhou Train in One Day 162

One Dead, One Injured

Yesterday morning at 9:45, the 40th slow passenger train from North Station to Hangzhou on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway ran over and killed a boy of about ten years old outside the Maigen Road Station around 10:00 AM. Because no one came to identify him, it is not known who he was. The station police notified the local bailiff to prepare a coffin for burial. At the same time, a freight train No. 552 from Zhapei to Gongchenqiao in the Zhapei-Gongchen District, when leaving Zhapei Station, ran over a girl of about the same age outside Waiyangqi. Her family lived near the railway house. Because the girl was playing stubbornly on the track and did not know how to avoid it, her mother took her to the nearby Zhapei Railway Medical Office for treatment.

Local News Two

All Parties Continue Disaster Relief 172

Requesting the China Western Jockey Club to Relief Shanghai to Raise

Funds for the Emergency Relief Association for Water Disasters in Various Provinces Yesterday, the China Western Jockey Club and the Jiangwan Jockey Club were asked to initiate disaster relief horse racing. The letter said: "We have long been aware of the widespread disaster, the large number of victims, and the tragic disaster situation in the water disasters in various provinces this year. Our association has initiated emergency relief fundraising without hesitation and has sent personnel to distribute them to disaster areas in various places. Since its establishment, it has been deeply grateful for the generous donations from all walks of life at home and abroad, including gentlemen, merchants, men and women, and overseas Chinese. The China Jockey Club held a Champagne Competition on October 25 and generously assisted our association with 200,000 silver dollars. Our association is deeply grateful for the club's enthusiasm. However, now that the severe winter is approaching, the victims in various provinces are suffering from hunger and cold and are waiting for relief. It is not enough to raise more funds to subsidize education. Your association has long had sympathy for disaster relief and drowning, so we specially send a letter to ask you to show great compassion and quickly donate or initiate a charity champagne or hold disaster relief horse racing. It is only a matter of raising your voice and reaching out your hand, but the victims will be greatly benefited and the dead will be brought back to life. We look forward to your kind help." In addition, the Shanghai Brick and Ash Industry Association handed in 1,355 yuan in collected donations. The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce replied with an introduction to place donation boxes in various companies and shops, and 111 letters of introduction were attached. The Suzhou Oriental Grand Theater sent a letter stating that a fundraising entertainment event will be held on the 13th, 14th, and 15th of this month and requested that personnel be sent to participate.

Decided to Stop Sheltering Disaster Victims

This Year. After the water disasters in various places, disaster victims have taken refuge in Shanghai and have been sheltered by the Disaster Victims Office. The office held a meeting yesterday and all the directors decided that no more disaster victims will be sheltered in the future. The disaster victims currently in Shanghai should still be sent back. The repatriation method will be negotiated by the office with Datong and Dada Shipping Companies. Ships will be sent daily to transport them free of charge. If they reach their original place of origin, the office will entrust the ship to transfer one yuan to them as a temporary living expense. At the same time, the local authorities are requested to find ways to earn a living. According to the statistics of the office yesterday, in addition to the 2,000 or more people who have been repatriated, there are still more than 6,000 people in Shanghai, most of whom are from Gaoyou, Xinghua, Shaobo, and other places in northern Jiangsu. The disaster victims from Hubei, Anhui, Jiangxi, and other provinces have been almost completely repatriated, and only a few hundred people remain. It is expected that about 400 disaster victims will be repatriated daily in the future and will be completed by the end of this month.

Central Relief for Northeast Arsenal

Workers The Central Relief Committee sent Mr. Chen Kui yesterday with funds to Qu Zhenren Temple to distribute the second batch of temporary relief funds of 4 yuan per person to the 16 workers (i.e., organized into the second regiment) of the Northeast Arsenal who were in distress and arrived in Shanghai. The distribution began at 11:00 AM. Mr. Zhu Yulin from the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau was present to supervise the distribution, and Zhou Inspector and Wang Inspector from the Public Security Bureau's 2nd District led the police to take care of the situation. The workers verified the symbols, issued the money, and the workers personally reported their names, ages, and native places, and filled in the form to sign for the money. The procedure was quite clear and ended at 3:00 PM. A total of 185 people were actually issued 740 yuan. There were still 30 people who were not issued due to absence, and they were ordered to come to the meeting to receive it in person tomorrow. A final photo will be taken for reference. Another 150 or so workers in distress in the third batch have also arrived in Shanghai and have been organized into the third regiment. They have been reported to the competent authorities for relief. Once they are verified, personnel will be sent to distribute them in the near future.

The 15th Standing Committee Meeting of the Anhui Relief

Association The Anhui Water Disaster Relief Association held its 15th Standing Committee Meeting yesterday. Chairman Xu Jingren reported on: (1) Letters from 24 counties including Nanling and Fuyang reporting on the receipt of funds and investigation forms; (2) Zhang Gongheng, a special commissioner sent by the National Government Water Disaster Relief Committee to Anhui, reported on the current situation of relief work in Anhui; (3) A letter from the Anhui Civil Affairs Department replied that it had issued an order to various counties to strictly prohibit brewing; (4) A letter from the Anhui Construction Department reported on the provincial government's handling of provincial road surcharges and the progress of its work for reference; (5) Reports on the fundraising situation from the Fujian Fellow Villagers Association and Commander Liu Heding; (6) A letter from Xu Pingxuan reported on the distribution of various relief funds he handled; (7) Reports from Zhu Runbin and E Runzhi on the accommodation of disaster victims in the shelter were received with sympathy from various charitable organizations in Shanghai. The following resolutions were made: (1) According to the reports from various counties, the Anhui Provincial Government is still strongly collecting a 30% construction surcharge. How should this be handled? The resolution was to check this case. Chairman Chen Tiaoyuan of the Provincial Government has agreed to stop collecting it. Now, there is still a situation of levy. A general letter should be sent to the various counties to stop paying uniformly, and the Provincial Government should be telegraphed again with serious questions, requesting that it issue an order to stop the levy immediately; (2) Various salt merchants in Wanzhi Town presented a complaint accusing the town's water disaster association of arbitrarily levying salt tax surcharges. Please correct it. The resolution was to reply to the complaint directly to the Provincial Relief Affairs Association; (3) Shou County telegraphed to request that the 1,500 yuan allocated by this association be transferred to work relief. The resolution was to reply to the situation in the local area and organize it as needed; (4) A telegram urged the Yi Tai Chamber of Commerce to quickly present the 1,000 yuan in relief funds previously remitted by this association for distribution to the most serious disaster area of Mingguang; (5) An additional 1,000 yuan was allocated to the Water Disaster Emergency Relief of the Anhui Fellow Villagers in Pengze and handed over to Xu Pingxuan for distribution; (6) A telegram requested the Anhui Civil Affairs Department to thoroughly investigate the historical situation of each county's accumulation and announce the amount of accumulated grain; (7) A letter was sent to the He County Government and Chamber of Commerce to persuade the county's pawnbrokers to show compassion for the disaster victims and exempt interest from the expired redemption and help with relief; (8) A letter replied to Wangjiang County, requesting that they prepare their own relief tickets and report the distribution situation to the association for record; (9) It was decided to invite Huang Binhong, Wang Yingbin, and Hong Jiesheng this Friday (November 6) to discuss the scheduling of a calligraphy and painting exhibition.

News of the Accumulation of Disaster Relief Wheat and Flour

The National Government Disaster Relief Committee has signed a contract with the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to lease the company's Pudong East Wharf and all its equipment free of charge for the loading, unloading, and storage of relief wheat and flour. The lease period is from the date of signing the contract to May 15 next year. During the lease period, all the normal expenses of the East Wharf will be borne by the Disaster Relief Committee.

The East Wharf has now been taken over by the Marine Transportation Division of the Disaster Relief Committee for management. The warehouse guards are filled by tax police transferred from the Salt Affairs Division.

The first batch of 7,000 tons of American wheat will arrive in Shanghai this week. The second batch is expected to arrive around the 12th of this month and will be directly transported to Ningbo for packaging and then transferred to the disaster area for distribution. The transportation matters in Hankou will be managed by the Hankou Subai Bank. Various procedures have been negotiated. The third, fourth, and fifth batches of American wheat will be directly transported to Hankou, and the sixth batch will be directly transported to Xunyang.

Son Sues Father 173

Petition for Alimony

Daughter-in-law Represents Father-in-law in Court

Judge Disapproves

Cai Ahu, a native of Chuansha, operates a prosperous dairy business at 45 Singapore Road. He has a son named Qiuquan, 33 years old, who is married to a Sun. Cai Qiuquan hired lawyer Dong Banggan to file a petition with the local court mediation office, requesting alimony. Due to Cai Ahu's absence, mediation was impossible. Cai Qiuquan then formally requested the court to order his father to pay alimony of 15,000 yuan, while also reserving his right to inheritance.

His petition stated: "I am the biological son of the defendant (Cai Ahu). However, my mother passed away long ago, and my stepmother, Madam Yang, is inherently malicious and skilled at sowing discord, leading the defendant to listen to slander and treat me with animosity. Not only does he disregard my livelihood, but on August 27th of this year, at 8:00 AM, the defendant gathered a group of people who forcibly tied me up and threw lime into my eyes. I struggled and shouted for help, fortunately, neighbors heard and arrived to prevent permanent injury. I sustained multiple injuries and was reported by the neighbors to the Gordon Road police station, who forwarded me to the First Special District Court for examination. The court determined the injuries and, upon the plaintiff's request for financial compensation instead of punishment, advised the defendant to allocate property for me to make a living. However, the defendant has not complied. Since the location falls under your jurisdiction, I specially petition for mediation, as the defendant is wealthy, owning a dairy farm on Singapore Road with 180 head of cattle, along with buildings and equipment, valued at approximately 100,000 yuan. He also owns over 400 mu of farmland in Shatien, Chuansha, valued at approximately 20,000 yuan, and has savings of over 10,000 yuan in HSBC and another 10,000 yuan in the Bank of Communications, as well as outstanding loans of over 70,000 yuan, totaling over 200,000 yuan in assets. Considering the bond between father and son, I have refrained from pursuing the assault. According to Article 1114 of the current Civil Code, lineal relatives have a mutual obligation to provide support, and according to Interpretation No. 2025 (Shang) of the fourth year of the Republic, the court may, upon the request of the parties, order the allocation of property. I am over 30 years old and have assisted in the defendant's dairy farm since childhood, without receiving adequate education and unable to perform strenuous work. Moreover, since the lime incident, my eyesight has not fully recovered despite numerous treatments. I am now homeless and facing starvation. The defendant, possessing immense wealth, heartlessly disregards my plight."

Yesterday morning, Judge Han Jingdou opened the trial. The defendant, Cai Ahu, did not appear, but was represented by his daughter-in-law, Cai Sun. The plaintiff recounted the previous events. Cai Sun stated that she was 32 years old. At this point, the plaintiff's lawyer interjected, stating that it was strange for Cai Sun, the plaintiff's wife, to represent her father-in-law. The judge also expressed disapproval and instructed Cai Sun that Cai Ahu must appear in person at the next hearing. She respectfully agreed and left.

Legacy Harms People 174

Brothers Actually Kill Each Other

Zhang Guoxiang and Yuxiang Killed

Done by Younger Brother Qingxiang

Originally Scheduled to Divide the Inheritance Yesterday

Leading to This Tragic Event the Night Before

Zhang Linsheng, the deceased compradore of the Swatow Wharf of the Taikoo Company, resided at 112 Huayuan Stone Bridge in Pudong. His sons, Guoxiang and Yuxiang, were assassinated by gunmen in front of the gate of Lane 35, No. 6, at approximately 7:00 PM the night before. Yuxiang was pronounced dead upon arrival at Renji Hospital. Guoxiang was sent to Baolong Hospital for treatment. This was reported in yesterday's newspaper.

The chief of the Third District Public Security Bureau, recognizing the threat to local security, immediately dispatched all officers to various ferries and checkpoints to inspect pedestrians and search for the murderers. By 9:00 PM, no suspects had been found. Rumors among nearby residents suggested that the case involved brothers killing each other over inheritance disputes. The district chief, believing that clues could be found, secretly dispatched police to Zhang's residence to investigate. They found Zhang Qingxiang (Guoxiang's second younger brother) and his mother, Madam Zhang (Linsheng's third wife), whispering inside the house. Qingxiang had loosened his long robe, appearing ready for sleep, showing no signs of grief. The police brought both Qingxiang and Madam Zhang to the district office for questioning.

Madam Zhang stated that she was 45 years old and that her husband, Linsheng, had passed away five years ago. His first wife, Madam Qian, died of illness in February of this year. Guoxiang, adopted, was 30 years old. She and Linsheng had three sons: Yuxiang, 23, who was adopted by Madam Qian; Qingxiang, 20; and Yunxiang, 18, who lived with her. The family property had been divided by her husband during his lifetime, but no written agreement had been made. The division was scheduled for the second (yesterday), but Guoxiang and Yuxiang were assassinated that evening for unknown reasons. She requested an investigation.

Qingxiang stated that he had been ill for several days and had just recovered. He went to play mahjong with friends east of Yangjing Temple at 8:00 AM and returned at 5:00 PM. He went out to buy shoes at around 7:00 PM and heard that his two elder brothers had been shot.

The district chief asked why, knowing that his brothers had been harmed, he had not immediately reported to the district office to pursue the murderers and send the injured to the hospital. His lack of grief and apparent readiness for sleep raised suspicions. He was advised to confess the truth to mitigate his crime. However, Qingxiang insisted that he was ill and unable to walk.

During the interrogation, a phone call from the Xinzha police station reported that Zhang Guoxiang had identified his younger brother, Qingxiang, as the murderer at Baolong Hospital. The district chief, convinced that the case was clear, ordered Zhang and Madam Zhang to be detained and sent to court for investigation.

Guoxiang's injury was caused by a bullet entering through the corner of his mouth and lodging in his throat. The injury was not fatal. He was able to speak yesterday. District Chief Zhang dispatched detectives Zhang Yong and Yang Jinsheng to Baolong Hospital for questioning. Guoxiang stated that he and his brother Yuxiang had returned home from a birthday dinner at Shunxing Restaurant in Lannidu at 7:00 PM. While changing clothes, as they passed the bamboo fence at No. 6 Lane 35, Yangjiazhai Road, someone jumped out from the darkness, shined a flashlight on his face, and fired a shot, hitting him in the corner of his mouth. Looking back, he recognized his third younger brother, Qingxiang. He fled in pain towards the street, hearing another shot, which hit the bamboo fence, followed by three or four more shots. He feared for his second brother Yuxiang's life. He also stated that his maternal uncle (Zhang's brother), Zhang Quansheng, who lived south of Sanguantang in Tangqiao, harbored deep resentment towards him and was likely involved in the case.

Detectives Zhang returned to the district office and notified the Tangqiao Third District Third Precinct by telephone, ordering the police to arrest Zhang Quansheng at his residence. Zhang Quansheng stated that he was 42 years old and currently the owner of the Yangtze River tugboat Dredging Company, a U.S. business, and had not been in contact with his sister for four years. He claimed to know nothing about the case. Under repeated interrogation, he admitted to possessing a large handgun, which he had exchanged for a four-inch handgun with Yang Fulin, a member of the Tangqiao District Security Corps. He claimed his wife had the gun.

The district chief, noting that two small handgun bullets, one live and one spent, matching the four-inch handgun, were found at the scene, became more suspicious and ordered him to be temporarily detained, pending a written report and the transfer of Zhang Qingxiang and Madam Zhang to court for further investigation today.

Yuxiang's body was taken away by family members at 10:00 PM that night. Yesterday morning, local security guard Xie Along reported the death to the local court. In the afternoon, Prosecutor Shen and others arrived in Pudong to examine the body. The examination confirmed that the deceased had been shot once in the right temple and once in the cheekbone, both fatal wounds. The prosecutor ordered the body to be prepared for burial by the widow, Madam Bao, pending further investigation by the police district.

Letter Threatening to Extort a Comprador 175

Suddenly a Letter Basket Appears on the Bamboo Fence

Intimidation, Extortion, Fake Urination

Arrest Due to Various Suspicions

On the morning of the 30th of last month, Wang Xinzhai, a native of Anhui and comprador of the Fuma Fur Export Company at 116 Jiangxi Road, residing at No. 5 Yong'an Lane, Bairbu Road, in the French Concession, received a threatening letter from the post office demanding 2,000 yuan. The letter instructed him to place the money in a paper basket on the bamboo fence opposite Ma'an Lane on Chongqing Road in the Public Concession between 6:00 PM and 7:00 PM on the 31st, and someone would retrieve it. Wang reported the matter to the Lujiawan police station.

On the afternoon of the 31st, detectives Jin Jiu, Lin Zheng, Qian Yumin, Mao Jingen, and Zhang Ziying of the special task force, along with plainclothes officers and representatives of the victim, arrived at the designated location on time. They found an old paper basket hanging on the bamboo fence with a narrow red strip of paper attached. The detectives placed a package of newspapers resembling banknotes into the basket and scattered to wait. At around 7:00 PM, a local man named Xu Azhao arrived, peeking back and forth several times. The detectives arrested him. His answers were evasive, and he was taken to the police station.

Yesterday afternoon, at 2:30 PM, the police station transferred Xu to the Second Criminal Court, where Judge Luo Renji conducted the trial. First, police lawyer Gu Shouxi presented the case, charging him under Article 370 of the Criminal Law. Detective Mao Jingen reported the arrest, stating that after the victim reported the letter, they went to the bamboo fence at 4:00 PM in the afternoon but found no paper basket. They returned at 6:00 PM and found a paper basket with a red paper marker. At 7:10 PM, the defendant arrived, pacing back and forth five or six times and pretending to urinate in the lane (without lowering his trousers). The arrest was made because his story about waiting for a woman to pick up clothes was completely inconsistent with the investigation. He claimed to be a carpenter at the tram company, but it was found that he was a carpenter at Feng Fa Ji carpentry shop.

The plaintiff, Wang Xinzhai, was out of town, so his representative, Rong Lisheng, appeared in court and recounted the circumstances of receiving the letter and reporting it to the police. Xu Azhao, 36 years old, residing next to a friend's place at 1162 Maho Road, Edward Avenue, claimed to be a plasterer. He stated that he had arranged to meet a woman there to pick up clothes and was looking for her address, denying any involvement in the extortion. Judge Luo, after reviewing the testimony, ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody pending further investigation and adjourned the hearing.

Sixteen-Year-Old Girl 176

Spending Six Nights with a Man

Afraid to Face Grandmother in Court

Hiring a Lawyer to Confess the Truth

Grandmother Says She Relies on Granddaughter to Live

Gong Qiaobao Confesses Adultery

Yan Wang, an old woman from Yangzhou residing at 367 Dong Youheng Road, reported that her sixteen-year-old granddaughter, Yan Meimei, a worker in a cigarette factory, disappeared suddenly at 5:00 AM on the 26th of last month. After searching without success, a relative and fellow townsman, Li Xiaoxizi, informed her that Yan Meimei was staying with a man named Gong Qiaobao (also from their hometown). Gong was willing to offer five yuan as betrothal money and choose an auspicious day for marriage. The grandmother refused, demanding the return of her granddaughter and reporting the matter to the Harbin police station. Detective Hou Fulin and a Western detective located Gong and Yan Meimei at Room 26 of the Zhongnan Hotel at 1914 Edward Avenue. They were found sleeping together. When awakened, they were arrested. Yan Meimei stated that she had been abused by her grandmother Wang and was willing to stay with Gong, refusing to return home. The police chief ordered Gong to be detained and Yan to be released, instructing her to appear in court the next day for questioning.

Yesterday morning, the police station transferred Gong Qiaobao to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin presented the case, stating that the defendant had admitted to spending six nights with Yan: the first night at the Yingbin Hotel on Fuzhou Road, the second and third nights at the home of the defendant's maternal uncle on Zhaofeng Road, and the fourth, fifth, and sixth nights at the Zhongnan Hotel. Yan Meimei did not appear. A lawyer appeared on her behalf, stating that Yan was afraid of being coerced by her grandmother Wang if she appeared in court today and would appear at the next hearing.

Yan Wang stated that she was 62 years old and had lost her son and daughter-in-law. Meimei was her granddaughter, working in a cigarette factory, and she relied on her for support. She did not trust the defendant and had heard that he was a dissolute son who had previously committed a crime. After her granddaughter disappeared, she found that her clothes had been taken, and she briefly described the situation, stating that she did not know where her granddaughter was. Zheng Wenkai was hired as the lawyer for the defendant.

Li Xiaoxizi stated that he had seen the defendant and the girl together at the Zhongnan Hotel. He had heard others say that Yan Wang wanted the defendant to pay 400 yuan to go abroad before allowing him to marry her, otherwise it was impossible. He had not relayed the defendant's offer of 50 yuan as betrothal money to Yan Wang.

The defendant stated that he and Yan had been classmates for five or six years and had become acquainted. She had been abused and driven out by the plaintiff Yan Wang, so she willingly followed him and spent six nights with him. He denied any previous adulterous relationship with her and pleaded for leniency. Judge Xiao Xiechen, after reviewing the testimony, ordered him to be remanded in custody and adjourned the hearing until Yan appeared in court for further questioning.

Record of Interrogation of the Kidnappers in the Zhu Yanqing Case 180

Zhu Yanqing, the owner of the Zhenhe Tea Shop in Dean Lane, North Shanxi Road, Public Concession, was abducted on the evening of September 8 while returning to his residence in Fangbanqiao, Huajie, in his private car. The abduction took place in front of Bulin Lane at the intersection of Zhengjiamuqiao Street and Minguo Road in the French Concession. He was hidden in a garret at 73 Jianye Lane, Fuli Road, with the intention of extorting a ransom. Detectives Jin Jiulin and Bao Tan of the Special Task Force of the French Concession Police investigated the case. On the 15th of the month, Zhu was rescued, and ten men and women, including Zheng A'er, Yu A'qing, Tang A'fu, Cao Zhang, Qian Taoyuan, Hong A'gen, Lu Yisheng, Wang Ziqing, Wang Zhang, Zhao, Liu, and Liu Ziqing, all from Tongzhou, were arrested and sent to the Second Special District Local Court for interrogation.

Yesterday was another day for the trial. The police brought the defendants to court. At 2:30 PM, Judge Luo Renji presided over the trial in the Second Criminal Court. The judge first ordered the victim, Zhu Yanqing, to appear in court and questioned him about the abduction and the conditions in the kidnappers' den. The judge then ordered the arguments to begin.

Police lawyer Gu Shouxi stood up and argued that the first defendant was the initiator of the case, instigated by the seventh defendant. The first defendant found the seventh defendant on September 3 and planned the kidnapping at 13 Jianye Lane, directing the other bandits on the scene, making him one of the main culprits. Although the second defendant was not present at the time of the kidnapping, he participated in the meeting and guarded the driver during the hijacking, making him also guilty of kidnapping. The third defendant participated in the kidnapping on the scene and also acted as a guard for the hostage, making him at least guilty of Article 373 of the Criminal Law. The fifth defendant was also an important figure in the case, having been notified first and asking Hong A'gen for help. Although he did not go to the kidnappers' den after the abduction, he was still culpable. Although the sixth defendant did not participate in the kidnapping on the scene, he acted as a lookout in the kidnappers' den and wrote a letter to the victim, contacting him at North Sichuan Road. The seventh defendant was the victim's former driver, who knew that Zhu was wealthy and instigated the kidnapping, making him the most important figure in the case. The eighth defendant went to rent a car after the meeting on September 3, acted as a lookout during the kidnapping, and contacted him about the ransom. The ninth and tenth defendants had relatively minor involvement. The eleventh defendant was present at the meeting and overturned Zhu's car during the kidnapping, making him an important figure in the case. He requested that the court punish him according to the law.

Lawyer Huang Xiubo was hired by Cao Zhang and Hong A'gen to defend them. Other lawyers including Wang Shizong, Xu Yannian, Lin Yingqing, Gu Changyuan, and Wu Youyuan, were appointed by the court to provide free legal representation for the defendants. They argued that the defendants were trapped by poverty and ignorance, and had fallen into the net of the law due to their ignorance, and asked the court to show leniency. Judge Luo announced the end of the arguments and scheduled the sentencing for the morning of the 9th of this month. The defendants were returned to custody.

Incoming Mail

The Origin of Photographically Reproducing the Song Dynasty Block-Printed Tripitaka 187

Since Buddhism was introduced to the East in the Han Dynasty, the two monks, Kasyapa Matanga and Dharmaratna, first translated the Sutra of Forty-two Sections and the Sutra on the Ten Stages of Disconnecting Ties. After that, the Wei, Jin, Six Dynasties, and even the Sui and Tang dynasties were engaged in translating the Tripitaka, with brilliant and complete texts. The preservation and circulation of scriptures only relied on stone carvings and handwriting. For example, the Shamen Jingwan in the Sui Dynasty created and carved the stone Tripitaka, which was sealed in Baitai Mountain in Fangshan County, Hebei Province. Stone carvings are still preserved here. For example, the Tang Dynasty's handwritten scriptures were recently discovered in the Dunhuang stone chamber. This is how handwriting was circulated. The art of woodblock printing began in the Five Dynasties and flourished in the Song Dynasty. In the fourth year of the Kaibao reign, Emperor Taizu ordered Zhang Congxin to carve the Tripitaka in Yizhou. It took thirteen years to complete it in the eighth year of the Taiping Xingguo reign of Emperor Taizong. It was called the Shu-printed edition, which was the beginning of carving the Tripitaka and was known as the Northern Song edition. Unfortunately, it has long been lost. Only fragments have been circulated in the world. Obtaining a single piece is worth a lot of money and is extremely valuable. In the second year of the Shaoxing reign of Emperor Gaozong of the Southern Song Dynasty, Wang Yong and his family from Huzhou vowed to carve the Tripitaka in Yuanjue Temple in Sixi, which was known as the Sixi edition. During the Jiaxi reign of Emperor Lizong, Yansheng Temple in Qisha also began to carve the Tripitaka, which was completed in the third year of the Zhida reign of Emperor Wuzong of the Yuan Dynasty. It was known as the Qisha edition. Both of these editions have seventeen characters per line and six lines per page. Only the lone copy in Xi'an, Shaanxi, China, remains.

Kang Youwei saw it in the past and wanted to reproduce and circulate it, but failed to do so. In the year of Gengwu, Qing Lan and others arrived in Xi'an to provide disaster relief. He was touched by the fact that Guanzhong was once a Buddhist center, but now the great law is declining and disasters are increasing. He thought of the opportunity to revive it. When he arrived at Wolong Temple and Kaiyuan Temple, he saw the complete Southern Song edition standing there. Checking the carving year, it was from the first year of the Duanping reign of Emperor Lizong of the Song Dynasty to the eleventh year of the Dade reign of Emperor Chengzong of the Yuan Dynasty. Although the volumes were vast and could not be checked one by one, it can be determined that it was the Qisha edition. The Buddha taught that the Three Treasures should be respected together, and the Dharma Treasure is especially important. Without the Dharma Treasure, the Buddha Treasure cannot be promoted, and the Sangha Treasure has nothing to rely on. Therefore, there is a proposal to photographically reproduce the Song Dynasty block-printed Tripitaka. The people of Shaanxi mostly agree, and even those in Shanghai invite the monks and lay people to plan the methods. They all agree that checking the block pieces for missing pieces is the first problem to be solved. It is also heard that the Songpo Library in Beiping also has fragments of the Song Tripitaka, so they first went to Beiping to borrow and read them. Knowing the number of volumes stored there, they also obtained a self-recording of the Song Tripitaka and went to Xi'an to check according to the list. They knew that the two places contained a total of 5,629 volumes in addition to the same ones. Only 173 volumes were missing. They searched other temples to see if they could find them. Otherwise, they would supplement them with the Ming Tripitaka to make a perfect collection. There are also precedents for this method. In the autumn of Xinwei, he gathered with his colleagues in Shanghai many times to discuss the fundraising and printing, and they had a clear plan. So the committee was organized to be responsible for the progress. The printing will be carried out by the Buddhist Scripture Bookstore, which is expected to be completed in three years. The grand event of reproducing the Qing Dynasty Dragon Tripitaka is now stored in Beiping. The price of each set is 5,000 yuan for paper, transportation, and other expenses. Those who are unable to do so are unable to do it. Now, the price of each set of the photographed Song Collection is only one-tenth of that of the Dragon Collection. It is easy to do, and each temple across the country will have a copy in the future, which is definitely not difficult. It makes one reason. Collectors of Song Dynasty books cherish them like jade. Recently, reproductions have been circulating, but only Buddhist scriptures are still missing. Now there are thousands of volumes in the world. It is not only for Buddhist followers to study, but also for those who are interested in ancient times. Its second convenience. Believers at home and abroad have heard the news and supported it

There must be someone. I would like to briefly describe the origin to the public. Initiators: Zhu Qinglan, Ye Gongchuo, Xu Shiying, Qu Yingguang, Shi Zhaozeng, Li Fan, Zhang Qiaoqing, Jiang Weiqiao, Di Baoxian, Ding Fubao, Chen Zhengyou, Wang Zhen, Huang Qinglan, Ouyang Jian, Chen Guangfu, Wu Yunzhai, Shi Jingcai, Kang Jiyao, Zha Liangzhao, Li Yunshu, Wan Shuhao, Shi Taixu, Shi Kecheng, Shi Fancheng, Li Zushen, Wu Jiqing, Ding Guilun, Lu Cheng, Ye Erkai, Xu Jiyu, Ni Wenqing, Jiang Du, Zhou Meiquan, Meng Chun, Sun Gaojie, Ren Yuan, Gu Nong, Zhang Yun, Li Yuanjing, Zhu Shiseng, Shen Binhan, and Li Jingwei.

Reader Correspondence 189

Mr. Zhong Xiehua's Message (A Respectful Announcement to All Volunteer Soldiers in the City):

(Today, what day is it? It is the sorrowful anniversary of one and a half months since the violent Japanese forcibly occupied Liaoning and Jilin! At this time when our land has not been recovered and our national humiliation has not been avenged, all volunteer soldiers in this city are holding a solemn oath-taking ceremony. The importance of the mission they bear is self-evident. Consider that the violent Japanese have recently continued to increase their troops in the Northeast, engaging in beastly acts without end, such as forcibly occupying railways, establishing artillery emplacements, building barracks, and digging trenches, constantly expanding their military operations to fulfill their delusional continental policy. Alas! While the enemy is deeply immersed in their beautiful dreams, may we suddenly awaken with a start, follow the League of Nations resolution, and implement the withdrawal of troops before the 16th, returning our rivers and mountains. Even a three-foot-tall child would know this is impossible. Therefore, the final battle against Japan is an unavoidable reality. All my beloved comrades in the army are vanguards of the people. Upon taking the solemn oath to defend our country's thousands of cities, they will set out to serve on the frontier, surely kill the enemy and achieve results, and recovering our rivers and mountains is within our grasp. However, Xiehua, based on his observations, cannot help but speak. During this solemn and awe-inspiring oath-taking ceremony, I also wish to discuss the following points with all my comrades in the army: (1) Obey Orders: An army that obeys orders is akin to a second life. An army that disobeys commands and disregards orders will never win on the battlefield. History, both domestic and foreign, proves this point. However, the virtue of obedience depends on the cultivation of regular habits. Therefore, the entire army must absolutely obey the orders of their superiors. (2) Intensify Training: All my comrades in the army have made the greatest determination to participate in training, sacrificing everything without hesitation. However, before training is fully mastered and actions are unified, we must not rashly engage the enemy and make unnecessary sacrifices that would deplete our national strength. Only by enhancing the entire army's combat capabilities can we achieve final victory. To achieve this goal, there is no other way than to strictly intensify training. Hereafter, I sincerely hope that my comrades in the army will not be late or absent unless absolutely necessary. (3) Mutual Respect and Love: All my comrades in the army are patriotic youths who deeply understand the great cause and voluntarily join the ranks, vowing to destroy the Japanese invaders. Their ambition is comparable to the sun and moon, and their spirit will be immortalized alongside the mountains and rivers. Therefore, all comrades in the army should show each other admiration and affection. Once ordered to kill the enemy, all soldiers should share weal and woe, and rely on each other for survival, surpassing even the bonds of brotherhood. In peacetime, how can we not strengthen unity through love, sincerity, and mutual encouragement? (4) Enduring Exercise: The "five-minute enthusiasm" is a stain on our entire nation. To remove this stain, everyone must painfully urge themselves to correct past mistakes in order to see results. Economic severance should be like this. War preparations should especially be like this permanently. Even if Japan partially withdraws its troops, and before our country implements conscription, the volunteer army should continue to expand its organization to contribute to the implementation of government conscription. The implementation of conscription has a significant impact on the country, especially in about five aspects. Please try to describe them: (1) Youths who receive military national education will surely be rich in the concept of loving the country and loving the nation. All bad habits can be swept away. (2) Everyone serving three to several years of military service will have firm will and strong physique. Even without seeking to strengthen the race, the race will naturally be strong. The infamous name of "sick man of the East" should be permanently separated from our great Republic of China. (3) Active duty soldiers must have received secondary education. Those who are illiterate will be given remedial education. Illiteracy can be gradually eliminated in the future, and education can be popularized. (4) The people of the whole country have clarified the purpose of the country raising soldiers, and are determined not to participate in civil wars. The self-destruction of internal fighting will never reappear in China after conscription. (5) Once war is declared against a foreign country, the whole country will be soldiers. With our nation's large population and the virtues of endurance and hard work, coupled with new-style weapons and strict training, we can directly be invincible and dominate the world. Is the small three islands worth one strike from our great Chinese nation? From these several points, we can see the arduous future responsibilities of the volunteer army and know where to strive. (5) Practicing Hard Work and Endurance: All my comrades in the army have dedicated themselves to the country and will not hesitate to break into pieces. What is there to fear of hardship? It is especially shameful for the very few people who are called "young masters." I secretly hope that this ominous nickname will never exist. Let us encourage each other with the words "practicing hard work and endurance." Xiehua is uneducated. The above points are based on what I have seen and I am not afraid to be vulgar and say everything in front of all my officers and brothers. If you adopt it, I should follow and encourage you to strive to implement it. (October 30th)

Weather Report 192

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the weather in the Yangtze River basin and coastal areas will be clear and cold, with fog in the morning. Moderate seasonal winds from the northwest to northeast will prevail along the coast of the country and in the Taiwan Strait. Free Talk

The Voice of Anti-Japanese Resistance

— Xu Xiaoting

Resisting Japanese goods is the responsibility of all people in the country. Everyone must have the determination to cooperate and resist forever.

The Chinese people are like a sheet of loose sand; no wonder they are looked down upon by the Japanese. But if everyone can unite from now on, they may be able to resist the violent Japanese.

What is justice? We Chinese believe it is something to rely on, but in reality, it is the self-comfort of a weak nation. In the eyes of the violent Japanese, it is like abandoned waste.

Instead of asking for international help because of the violent Japanese, we should encourage ourselves to do arduous work.

The Remaining Steles in Qingyang, Wuzhong 193

— Zheng Yimei

Qingyang is located outside the Panmen gate of Suzhou. During the late Qing Dynasty, it became a commercial port due to the Shimonoseki Treaty with Japan. At that time, Qingyang was the most prosperous area in the entire county, with shops lined up closely and brothels seemingly as numerous as clouds. In the past, people said, "Beyond the Changmen gate and past Panmalu, a weeping willow hangs over a painted building." The scenic beauty of the beaded curtains and ten miles of smoke and flowers was unsurpassed. Unexpectedly, things changed dramatically. The long-distance train tracks between Beijing and Shanghai were rapidly built. Train stations were set up outside the Changmen gate. As a result, the orioles and swallows of Qingyang dispersed, and merchants moved, competing to flock to Daiqiao and Changting, which suddenly became bustling markets. Qingyang gradually became desolate. The ancient road and setting sun only saw shepherd boys wandering. Although the Japanese tried hard to revive it, they specially opened Tongyin Garden in the summer to attract tourists, but because the location was remote, few people came to enjoy the scenery, and it eventually closed due to insufficient funds. The proverb "cold water Panmen" had long been known for a reason. However, every year during the late spring season, the sides of the road near the Japanese consulate were planted with cherry blossoms, white as snow. Many elegant scholars and poets came here to comment and appreciate them, and to mourn at the nearby Song Dynasty Grasshopper Tomb and the Han Dynasty General Who Conquered the Xiongnu, Sun Jian, and the tomb of Wu's wife, General Ce. Recently, someone from Qingyang, Wuzhong, said that a household in the area dug a well and found a stone tablet. After rubbing it, the inscription could be identified as: (The melancholy of the chaotic world is soaring, the rivers and seas are tumbling, and the mountains are shaking. The bugle calls in the morning and the horns sound at night. The general is angry and eight flags flee.) The part below was damaged and the words are unknown, nor is there any date or inscription. It seems to be a hidden prophecy of today's Japanese pirates. The words are ancient and vigorous and can be recited, but the phrase "The general is angry and eight flags flee" is obscure and its meaning is unknown. I will record it first so that I can observe whether it will be fulfilled in the future.

Record of the Shanghai Volunteer Army Oath-Taking and Grand Review 194

— Rui Zhaoji

This time, the violent Japanese invaded our Northeast and massacred our compatriots, causing pain and indignation throughout the country. Mr. Ye Huijun, Mr. Li Cishan, Mr. Chen Yafu and other famous people in Shanghai were filled with righteous indignation and specially organized the Shanghai Anti-Japanese Salvation Volunteer Army. The number of people who signed up was endless, reaching over 10,000, willing to meet the Japanese invaders on the battlefield to fight to the death. They have been practicing combat exercises at the crack of dawn for several days, and the results have been quite good. The oath-taking ceremony was held on November 1st at the Public Sports Ground on Dajilu, Ximen. I went there at 4:00 AM. The sky had not yet broken, and the cold wind was biting, but the volunteer soldiers had already arrived solemnly, showing a glimpse of their spirit. The oath-taking ceremony was held at around 9:00 AM. Having returned from the meeting, I will record my observations and experiences as follows:

Arrangement of the Venue: A reed shed was built high in the venue to serve as the command platform. Two wireless telephones were set up on both sides for broadcasting. Chinese Boy Scouts maintained order in the venue in an orderly manner.

Raising the Flag and Firing Cannons: At 10:00 AM, the national flag was raised and firecrackers were set off. The blue sky and white sun flag shone on the earth, symbolizing the overthrow of Japanese imperialism.

Inspection by Important Figures: More than 10,000 volunteer soldiers lined up and marched forward. Figures from the military and political circles, as well as Ye Huijun, Li Cishan, Chen Yafu, and others, stood around to inspect the solemn atmosphere.

Oath-Taking Ceremony: After the inspection, all committee members, officers, and soldiers took the oath. Representatives from the Central Training Headquarters, Garrison Headquarters, City Party Headquarters, Municipal Government, and Anti-Japanese National Salvation organizations all gave speeches.

Busy Photography: Reporters from Shen Bao and Shi Bao newspapers held cameras and were extremely busy taking pictures. Lianhua Film Company was also present to film.

Liangjiang Rescue: Ms. Gu Lihua, Principal of Liangjiang Women's Physical Education School, organized a rescue team and led all the female rescuers to the venue. They wore white cloth rhombus hats with a red cross in the middle and long white cloth shirts with numbers. Once they are on the battlefield, they will rely on these ladies for rescue.

Model Soldiers: The Second District of the Volunteer Army has made rapid progress in gymnastics. Their steps are neat and their appearance is magnificent. They can be called model volunteer soldiers.

Singing the Party Song: After the oath-taking ceremony, all the soldiers paraded while the military music was melodious and they sang the Party Song ("The Three Principles of the People, the foundation of our Party, to build the Republic of China and advance to the Great Harmony. You, many talented people, are the vanguard of the people, working tirelessly day and night, following the principles, swearing to be diligent, brave, faithful, and loyal, with one heart and one mind from beginning to end.") Finally, there was a photo session and the meeting was adjourned.

World Anecdotes 195

— Haike

A New Invention to Isolate Sounds: Those who live in the city are always surrounded by the noises of people, cars, and horses. It is really headache-inducing, and it is possible to shorten their lifespans. Therefore, it is a good idea to isolate yourself from the noises outside. Recently, the American Mr. H. Maxim invented something like that, and he recently had a public test in New York, and the results were very good. In recent years, tests like this have been done many times, but they could only be applied to new houses. It is difficult to isolate sounds by putting something between the walls and the outside. If you wanted to apply this to an existing house, you would have to rebuild it. However, Mr. Maxim's invention can be installed in an existing house without this trouble. Therefore, this is much better than previous inventions. Most doctors say that sounds have a very big effect on people's nerves. Therefore, hospitals welcome Mr. Maxim's invention, so that the patients can rest peacefully and will not be bothered by the city's noises, which will affect their health.

Drama and Reality 196

— Jian Xing

Yesterday, I went to Hechengtengfu for business and went to the North Station to buy a ticket and board the train. After a while, the bells rang and the train wheels rumbled, and the vendors on the train began to do business, and the newspaper business was even more prosperous than usual, because everyone was eager to see the news from the Northeast because of the Japanese atrocities and the national crisis.

An old man in the next seat had a bald head and missing teeth. Judging from his appearance, he was like a mediocre scholar, but he was very talkative. He was talking about current affairs with a small fat man, strongly criticizing the Chinese people for not being consistently patriotic. He said that the Chinese people were like sleepy idlers who did not notice when mosquitoes sucked their blood or fleas bit their skin. Only when rats gnawed at their toes and the pain was severe did they wake up and scold the rats. When the rats retreated slightly, they went back to sleep as before. The rats knew they were sleepy, so they gnawed at their thighs or bit their arms. The sleepy man woke up and went back to sleep, angrily scolding the rats but not thinking about how to prevent them. Now the rats have occupied his thighs and made them their nests. Although the sleepy man is angry and roars wildly, because he has been tormented by the rats for a long time and because he is sleepy and has internal diseases all over his body, he has no strength to drive away the rats and only calls for help from his neighbors. But the rats are secretly laughing and will soon fall asleep again. Although the words are extreme, they cannot be said to be inappropriate. Then the old man changed his tone and went from national affairs to his family affairs. The old man has a son named Jia in Shanghai who drives a car for a certain mansion and is in love with a dancer, and they have recently started living together. Jia's wife in his hometown did not know about this, but her neighbors who returned from Shanghai revealed the matter. The wife was very angry and went to Jia's residence in Shanghai and cried and shouted. At first, Jia deceived the dancer that he was not married, but now the dancer knew that she had been deceived by Jia and scolded Jia for being ungrateful. Jia was extremely angry and slapped his wife's face, but the wife turned around and went straight to the Huangpu River and committed suicide. The dancer then accused Jia of enticement in court. Now Jia is imprisoned and awaiting trial. The old man's trip was for this matter. He sighed and said no more. I felt that this matter was quite similar to the plot of the new silent film "Spring Colors on the Stage," but the methods were slightly different. In "Spring Colors on the Stage," the singer Li Huifang, after talking with Gui Bao and knowing the secrets of her lover, was overwhelmed with grief and indignation. However, her expression when she returned the diamond ring and rescued Gui Bao showed her great personality. The dancer's accusation against Jia for seduction was also very satisfying and served as a warning to those who deceive women. As for Jia and Zhang Xiaorong in "Spring Colors on the Stage," their behavior of forgetting the old for the new was ruthless and unjust, and Jia's wife and Gui Bao's misfortune in meeting the wrong person and having a short life were no different. Therefore, I know that all kinds of facts in the world can be made into dramas, and the plots in dramas are also the facts of the world.

Wang Jiyuan's Tour of Europe 197

— Yu Sao

Over the past month, Mr. Wang Jiyuan held a European tour exhibition at the Mingfu Library and the Bank Association Club. More than 8,000 people visited the exhibition, and 14 pieces of artwork were sold. Viewers praised him for it. Wang was inspired by well-known figures such as Matisse, Pica, and Staron during his time in Paris. He was made aware that all these well-known figures had different styles because each person had their own unique expression. All people are different and do not need to be the same. If they are the same, it is the same as a machine. Wang worked hard to innovate, and worked at the Grand Chaomi Institute and the Gera Laoshi Institute. People saw that Wang had unique strokes, simple lines, and sharp lines. Le Linearismeaiguetsimple is able to contend with the skills of the Japanese artist Foujita. Wang enjoyed being close to nature, and painting churches, famous gardens, European figures. People would stretch their necks to watch, as if he was the god of victory. (Water Pool), (Little Arc de Triomphe), (Viewing the Stove), (In Front of the Jiling Temple), (Street), (White Wall), (Snow Forest), (Fisherman), (Drizzle), (Sunset Glow), (Light Mist), (Winter Day), (Early Autumn), (Early Morning) and so on. All of these paintings were moving, and showed strong emotions and color. Not only did these figures have shapes, but they also showed the essence of the universe. Spring, Summer, Autumn, Winter, morning, noon, evening, and rain were vividly shown. The European merchants, students, church members, and vagabonds that he painted were also vivid. Some people always complain about Chinese art, and pay more attention to Western styles and techniques. People do not know that the artist needs to quickly capture the lightning-fast moments. In addition, the beauty of art is the style and not the details. If everyone adds unnecessary details, it is the same as forcing Kang Youwei to learn how to be a clerk, or forcing Wu Changshuo to be a painter.

In August 1930, Wang visited Belgium and participated in the World Expo, spending a month there and bringing back more than 40 pieces of artwork. In January of this year, he organized an exhibition at the Galerie Barreiro in Paris, which was well received and praised by Europeans. The critic Charles Fegdal said that he used Western impressionism, perspective, and techniques to paint the East.

Wang originally wanted to go to Berlin and London for long-term travel, but unfortunately, he suffered a foot disease when he arrived in Frankford and had to return to Paris. Soon, his friend Ye Yun, a student at the Ecole des Beaux-Arts in Paris, introduced Miss Wan, an Italian, and a Spanish dancer to his residence to serve as models for (Hesitation), (Looking in the Mirror), (Girl) and so on. Wang would not abandon even a moment. This fall, he returned to China and created dozens of works on the way. After arriving in Shanghai, he continued to study at the Art Garden. His spirit can be used as a good model for future generations. (Relocate to Help Revitalize)

A Discussion of Shrimp and Crab Disasters 198

— Qing Zao

Shrimp and crabs are both arthropods in the aquatic world. Although they have different shapes, they are of the same type. Shrimp produced in April and May are called (Seasonal Shrimp). They are transparent and taste very fresh. Crabs that are on the market after this time are called (June King). Although they are not fat, their taste is palatable. Lovers often compete to buy them to satisfy their appetites. However, the production of these two items varies from year to year. Therefore, our county has a saying: (Shrimp disasters and crab chaos). I don't know how this omen was obtained. It is probably the common sense passed down by the elders of the past.

This year, there are more shrimp than in the past. From the first half of the year to the present, there are almost no days when they are not abundant in the market. In the past, the price of each catty was more than one thousand copper coins. Now, half of that amount can be obtained. Crabs are also the same, but there are still more supplies than demand. If you go to the market to see, they are almost everywhere. It is also strange. However, our county's agricultural production has always been known for its cotton being seven parts and rice being three parts. Since the continuous rain has caused disaster, the cotton has flowers but no bells. Even if we want to change to planting other things, it is not possible. The rice harvest is later, and the autumn harvest is only 30% of the total county's harvest. Therefore, since this month, farmers from the four villages have been reporting disasters in the city, arriving at the county court day after day, many to more than a thousand and few to hundreds. County Magistrate Pan Gengsheng is suffering from this. Each person is given one hundred pennies, but those who come continue to come in an endless stream, and there are even those who are not farmers but are profiting from this district. Reluctantly, after giving the money, the palm is watermarked to distinguish it so that it does not come again. It is also ridiculous.

Those who know say that shrimp is a sign of many years of disaster, and that the abundance of crabs is a good sign. There are wars in the country, almost in proportion to the rise and fall of crabs. In the past, the crab market did not reach September, and the circular navel of October was gradually scarce. Even if there were, the price was expensive, and non-gourmets could not easily afford them. At this time, there is still an increase without a decrease. According to the crab catchers, each night a net can catch dozens of catties, and those who plant broken hats in the water can catch even more. The rumors about crab chaos are believed by those who talk about it. In this year of national disaster and famine, everyone uses this as a common saying. Therefore, I have specially recorded one or two of them. I think it is not only our county that has this phenomenon, but other places must also have it. Is there a definite relationship between the omens of good and bad luck and the nature of things?

The Rotary Club of Novels

The Countryman Visits Shanghai Again (5) 199

— Bao Tianxiao

The countryman thought, (When it comes to farming, you have to consult us countrymen. As the saying goes, "Confused, confused, soak rice seeds in the sixth month of the lunar calendar." If the rice seedling planting committee is sent down in the seventh month of the lunar calendar, that's just like the saying, "Soak rice seeds in the sixth month of the lunar calendar." No wonder those big shots spend the whole year fighting battles and discussing national affairs. This kind of farming is done by us barefoot people. They don't have the time to manage it.) The countryman was just explaining to himself when he suddenly heard a rumbling sound. Everyone shouted,

(The train is coming!) (The train is coming!)

The countryman recognized that this was a third-class car. He used to take the fourth-class car, and he saw that the outside of the car had four vertical marks. Now that he was taking the third-class car, it had three vertical marks. He thought that the car for livestock was probably a five vertical mark. He followed the crowd, pushing and shoving, into the third-class car. As soon as he stepped in, he was so frightened that he backed out. (I went to the wrong place! This is not a third-class car!)

(Who says it's not a third-class car?) said one of the people who went in with him.

(That's not right! I'm afraid this is a sleeping car, right?) The countryman was still hesitant to go in.

(Bah! How can there be sleeping cars during the day?) Of course, this person's experience with taking trains was more informed than the countryman's.

(Then why are there so many people sleeping in the car?)

Sure enough, in that third-class car, people were sleeping head to head and feet to feet, stretched out and lying down. That car was not a row of chairs, but strips of chairs. Because everyone was crowded into the first few third-class cars, these last few third-class cars were very empty. People who take the train are unwilling to have space in the car, probably a common psychology. Therefore, people who sit in the second-class car, who were originally supposed to sit two people in one chair, would also lie down and occupy the space when they saw an empty chair. They also saw that there was space in the first-class car, so people who sat in the second-class car also felt it was a pity and often went to the first-class car to occupy that space. Now that people in the third-class car see an empty seat next to them, why wouldn't they turn their bodies to occupy a few more seats?

Not only that, but there was a long shelf above the third-class car for passengers to put their luggage. Now that there were fewer passengers, there was naturally less luggage. Two friends in yellow pants arched their buttocks and slept on it, really like sleeping in a car, with high and low bunks. No wonder the countryman mistakenly thought he had walked into a sleeping car.

Finance 200

The Gold Market Continues to Decline

No Change in Half a Day. Yesterday (the 2nd), the posted gold price remained weak, with only slight fluctuations and no special changes. The market was only moderately active four or five times, and then finally fell by one or two taels. The industry was generally calm and there was not much trading volume. It was almost the same as the day before. The market continued to rise, opening lower and breaking 690 taels. Afterwards, buyers were keen as the foreign exchange market was apparently flat but secretly flexible. Banks were still able to accept inflows, and the market situation slightly stabilized. The price initially rose to ninety-two or three taels. Later in the day, the market was closed according to regulations due to the Western autumn horse racing season.

Opening Fell More Than Five Taels. It fell five taels and two qian from the early opening to six hundred eighty-nine and a half taels. The large bars then rose eight-tenths of a qian, and the forward contract rose sixteen-fifths. The silver price only rose one-eighth. However, recently, expectations of a price drop led to an unexpected rise, and people’s sentiments lowered. Furthermore, Shunli, Dadecheng, Wanxing, and others all sold off, followed by eighty-eight taels and five qian. In a short period, Yongfeng Zhifeng Yong bought in, immediately adding twelve taels to ninety taels and five qian. The English exchange rate did not change, and the gold squeeze small exchange rate decreased by one-two-five. Only because the autumn race was half an hour early, the announcement was made at nine o’clock. Fuchang Bingxing Yu Da Hengchang Jing and others also continued to rise to ninety-three taels and two qian. Da Hing Yong Zhifeng Yong Hui ○ Futai Heng and others sold, and it was heard that Indian merchants were selling one-month English gold at one eight three one two five, so it retreated two taels or so. At nine-thirty, it was ninety-one taels and three qian. At that time, there were only a few qian up and down. Subsequently, HSBC ate U.S. dollars for this month at thirty-two yuan five, which had already pulled up one and a half taels to ninety-two taels and eight qian. In a short while, HSBC sold a regular portion of thirty-two yuan five six two five, which was bought by American, Japanese and other banks.
